Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-110 Clearing corporation rules.
-----------------------------------------------------------
A rule adopted by a clearing corporation governing rights and obligations among the clearing corporation and its participants in the clearing corporation is effective even if the rule conflicts with this chapter and affects another party who does not consent to the rule.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-111 Creditor's legal process.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-111(1): (4) The interest of a debtor in a certificated security may be reached by a creditor only by actual seizure of the security certificate by the officer making the attachment or levy, except as otherwise provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-111(2): (4) The interest of a debtor in an uncertificated security may be reached by a creditor only by legal process upon the issuer at its chief executive office in the United States, except as otherwise provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-111(3): (4) The interest of a debtor in a security entitlement may be reached by a creditor only by legal process upon the securities intermediary with whom the debtor's securities account is maintained, except as otherwise provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-111(4): The interest of a debtor in a certificated security for which the certificate is in the possession of a secured party, or in an uncertificated security registered in the name of a secured party, or a security entitlement maintained in the name of a secured party, may be reached by a creditor by legal process upon the secured party.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-111(5): A creditor whose debtor is the owner of a certificated security, uncertificated security, or security entitlement is entitled to aid from a court of competent jurisdiction, by injunction or otherwise, in reaching the certificated security, uncertificated security, or security entitlement or in satisfying the claim by means allowed at law or in equity in regard to property that cannot readily be reached by other legal process.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-112 Statute of frauds inapplicable.
---------------------------------------------------------------
A contract or modification of a contract for the sale or purchase of a security is enforceable whether or not there is a writing signed or record authenticated by a party against whom enforcement is sought, even if the contract or modification is not capable of performance within one year of its making.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-113 Evidentiary rules concerning certificated securities.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The following rules apply in an action on a certificated security against the issuer:Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-113(1): Unless specifically denied in the pleadings, each signature on a security certificate or in a necessary indorsement is admitted.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-113(2): If the effectiveness of a signature is put in issue, the burden of establishing effectiveness is on the party claiming under the signature, but the signature is presumed to be genuine or authorized.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-113(3): If signatures on a security certificate are admitted or established, production of the certificate entitles a holder to recover on it unless the defendant establishes a defense or a defect going to the validity of the security.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-113(4): If it is shown that a defense or defect exists, the plaintiff has the burden of establishing that the plaintiff or some person under whom the plaintiff claims is a person against whom the defense or defect cannot be asserted.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-114 Securities intermediary and others not liable to adverse claimant.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A securities intermediary that has transferred a financial asset pursuant to an effective entitlement order, or a broker or other agent or bailee that has dealt with a financial asset at the direction of its customer or principal, is not liable to a person having an adverse claim to the financial asset, unless the securities intermediary, or broker or other agent or bailee:Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-114(1): took the action after it had been served with an injunction, restraining order, or other legal process enjoining it from doing so, issued by a court of competent jurisdiction, and had a reasonable opportunity to act on the injunction, restraining order, or other legal process; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-114(2): acted in collusion with the wrongdoer in violating the rights of the adverse claimant; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-114(3): in the case of a security certificate that has been stolen, acted with notice of the adverse claim.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-115 Securities intermediary as purchaser for value.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A securities intermediary that receives a financial asset and establishes a security entitlement to the financial asset in favor of an entitlement holder is a purchaser for value of the financial asset.  A securities intermediary that acquires a security entitlement to a financial asset from another securities intermediary acquires the security entitlement for value if the securities intermediary acquiring the security entitlement establishes a security entitlement to the financial asset in favor of an entitlement holder.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-201 Issuer.
---------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-201(1): With respect to an obligation on or a defense to a security, an "issuer" includes a person that:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-201(1)(a): places or authorizes the placing of its name on a security certificate, other than as authenticating trustee, registrar, transfer agent, or the like, to evidence a share, participation, or other interest in its property or in an enterprise, or to evidence its duty to perform an obligation represented by the certificate;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-201(1)(b): creates a share, participation, or other interest in its property or in an enterprise, or undertakes an obligation, that is an uncertificated security;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-201(1)(c): directly or indirectly creates a fractional interest in its rights or property, if the fractional interest is represented by a security certificate; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-201(1)(d): becomes responsible for, or in place of, another person described as an issuer in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-201(2): With respect to an obligation on or defense to a security, a guarantor is an issuer to the extent of its guaranty, whether or not its obligation is noted on a security certificate.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-201(3): With respect to a registration of a transfer, issuer means a person on whose behalf transfer books are maintained.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-202 Issuer's responsibility and defenses -- Notice of defect or defense.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-202(1): Even against a purchaser for value and without notice, the terms of a certificated security include terms stated on the certificate and terms made part of the security by reference on the certificate to another instrument, indenture, or document or to a constitution, statute, ordinance, rule, regulation, order, or the like, to the extent the terms referred to do not conflict with terms stated on the certificate.  A reference under this subsection does not of itself charge a purchaser for value with notice of a defect going to the validity of the security, even if the certificate expressly states that a person accepting it admits notice.  The terms of an uncertificated security include those stated in any instrument, indenture, or document or in a constitution, statute, ordinance, rule, regulation, order, or the like, pursuant to which the security is issued.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-202(2): (2)(a) The following rules apply if an issuer asserts that a security is not valid:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-202(2)(a): A security other than one issued by a government or governmental subdivision, agency, or instrumentality, even though issued with a defect going to its validity, is valid in the hands of a purchaser for value and without notice of the particular defect unless the defect involves a violation of a constitutional provision.  In that case, the security is valid in the hands of a purchaser for value and without notice of the defect, other than one who takes by original issue.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-202(2)(b): (2)(a) Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-202(3): 70A-8-205 Except as otherwise provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-202(4): All other defenses of the issuer of a security, including nondelivery and conditional delivery of a certificated security, are ineffective against a purchaser for value who has taken the certificated security without notice of the particular defense.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-202(5): This section does not affect the right of a party to cancel a contract for a security "when, as and if issued" or "when distributed" in the event of a material change in the character of the security that is the subject of the contract or in the plan or arrangement pursuant to which the security is to be issued or distributed.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-202(6): If a security is held by a securities intermediary against whom an entitlement holder has a security entitlement with respect to the security, the issuer may not assert any defense that the issuer could not assert if the entitlement holder held the security directly.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-203 Staleness as notice of defect or defense.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
After an act or event, other than a call that has been revoked, creating a right to immediate performance of the principal obligation represented by a certificated security or setting a date on or after which the security is to be presented or surrendered for redemption or exchange, a purchaser is charged with notice of any defect in its issue or defense of the issuer, if the act or event:Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-203(1): requires the payment of money, the delivery of a certificated security, the registration of transfer of an uncertificated security, or any of them on presentation or surrender of the security certificate, the money or security is available on the date set for payment or exchange, and the purchaser takes the security more than one year after that date; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-203(2): (1) is not covered by Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-204 Effect of issuer's restriction on transfer.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
A restriction on transfer of a security imposed by the issuer, even if otherwise lawful, is ineffective against a person without knowledge of the restriction unless:Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-204(1): the security is certificated and the restriction is noted conspicuously on the security certificate; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-204(2): the security is uncertificated and the registered owner has been notified of the restriction.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-205 Effect of unauthorized signature on security certificate.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
An unauthorized signature placed on a security certificate before or in the course of issue is ineffective, but the signature is effective in favor of a purchaser for value of the certificated security if the purchaser is without notice of the lack of authority and the signing has been done by:Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-205(1): an authenticating trustee, registrar, transfer agent, or other person entrusted by the issuer with the signing of the security certificate or of similar security certificates, or the immediate preparation for signing of any of them; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-205(2): (1) an employee of the issuer, or of any of the persons listed in Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-206 Completion or alteration of security certificate.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-206(1): If a security certificate contains the signatures necessary to its issue or transfer but is incomplete in any other respect:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-206(1)(a): any person may complete it by filling in the blanks as authorized; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-206(1)(b): even if the blanks are incorrectly filled in, the security certificate as completed is enforceable by a purchaser who took it for value and without notice of the incorrectness.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-206(2): A complete security certificate that has been improperly altered, even if fraudulently, remains enforceable, but only according to its original terms.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-207 Rights and duties of issuer with respect to registered owners.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-207(1): Before due presentment for registration of transfer of a certificated security in registered form or of an instruction requesting registration of transfer of an uncertificated security, the issuer or indenture trustee may treat the registered owner as the person exclusively entitled to vote, receive notifications, and otherwise exercise all the rights and powers of an owner.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-207(2): This chapter does not affect the liability of the registered owner of a security for a call, assessment, or the like.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-208 Effect of signature of authenticating trustee, registrar, or transfer agent.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-208(1): A person signing a security certificate as authenticating trustee, registrar, transfer agent, or the like, warrants to a purchaser for value of the certificated security, if the purchaser is without notice of a particular defect, that:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-208(1)(a): the certificate is genuine;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-208(1)(b): the person's own participation in the issue of the security is within the person's capacity and within the scope of the authority received by the person from the issuer; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-208(1)(c): the person has reasonable grounds to believe that the certificated security is in the form and within the amount the issuer is authorized to issue.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-208(2): (1) Unless otherwise agreed, a person signing under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-209 Issuer's lien.
----------------------------------------------
A lien in favor of an issuer upon a certificated security is valid against a purchaser only if the right of the issuer to the lien is noted conspicuously on the security certificate.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-210 Overissue.
------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-210(1): In this section, "overissue" means the issue of securities in excess of the amount the issuer has corporate power to issue, but an overissue does not occur if appropriate action has cured the overissue.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-210(2): (3); (4) Except as otherwise provided in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-210(3): If an identical security not constituting an overissue is reasonably available for purchase, a person entitled to issue or validation may compel the issuer to purchase the security and deliver it if certificated or register its transfer if uncertificated, against surrender of any security certificate the person holds.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-210(4): If a security is not reasonably available for purchase, a person entitled to issue or validation may recover from the issuer the price the person or the last purchaser for value paid for it with interest from the date of the person's demand.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-301 Delivery.
-----------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-301(1): Delivery of a certificated security to a purchaser occurs when:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-301(1)(a): the purchaser acquires possession of the security certificate;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-301(1)(b): another person, other than a securities intermediary, either acquires possession of the security certificate on behalf of the purchaser or, having previously acquired possession of the certificate, acknowledges that it holds for the purchaser; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-301(1)(c): a securities intermediary acting on behalf of the purchaser acquires possession of the security certificate, only if the certificate is in registered form and is:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-301(1)(c)(i): registered in the name of the purchaser;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-301(1)(c)(ii): payable to the order of the purchaser; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-301(1)(c)(iii): specially indorsed to the purchaser by an effective indorsement and has not been indorsed to the securities intermediary or in blank.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-301(2): Delivery of an uncertificated security to a purchaser occurs when:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-301(2)(a): the issuer registers the purchaser as the registered owner, upon original issue or registration of transfer; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-301(2)(b): another person, other than a securities intermediary, either becomes the registered owner of the uncertificated security on behalf of the purchaser or, having previously become the registered owner, acknowledges that it holds for the purchaser.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-302 Rights of purchaser.
----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-302(1): (2); (3) Except as otherwise provided in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-302(2): A purchaser of a limited interest acquires rights only to the extent of the interest purchased.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-302(3): A purchaser of a certificated security who as a previous holder had notice of an adverse claim does not improve its position by taking from a protected purchaser.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-303 Protected purchaser.
----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-303(1): "Protected purchaser" means a purchaser of a certificated or uncertificated security, or of an interest in the security, who:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-303(1)(a): gives value;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-303(1)(b): does not have notice of an adverse claim to the security;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-303(1)(c): obtains control of the security; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-303(1)(d): for a share of stock issued by a land company or a water company:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-303(1)(d)(i): pays, or whose predecessors in interest paid, an assessment levied against the share of stock for at least four of the immediate past seven years by the land company or the water company; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-303(1)(d)(ii): has used, or whose predecessors in interest have used, either directly or indirectly, the water available under the share of stock issued by a water company for at least four of the immediate past seven years.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-303(2): In addition to acquiring the rights of a purchaser, a protected purchaser acquires the purchaser's interest in the certificated or uncertificated security, share of stock in a land company, or share of stock in a water company free of any adverse claim.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-304 Indorsement.
--------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-304(1): An indorsement may be in blank or special.  An indorsement in blank includes an indorsement to bearer.  A special indorsement specifies to whom a security is to be transferred or who has power to transfer it.  A holder may convert a blank indorsement to a special indorsement.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-304(2): An indorsement purporting to be only of part of a security certificate representing units intended by the issuer to be separately transferable is effective to the extent of the indorsement.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-304(3): An indorsement, whether special or in blank, does not constitute a transfer until delivery of the certificate on which it appears or, if the indorsement is on a separate document, until delivery of both the document and the certificate.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-304(4): If a security certificate in registered form has been delivered to a purchaser without a necessary indorsement, the purchaser may become a protected purchaser only when the indorsement is supplied.  However, against a transferor, a transfer is complete upon delivery and the purchaser has a specifically enforceable right to have any necessary indorsement supplied.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-304(5): An indorsement of a security certificate in bearer form may give notice of an adverse claim to the certificate, but it does not otherwise affect a right to registration that the holder possesses.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-304(6): 70A-8-107 Unless otherwise agreed, a person making an indorsement assumes only the obligations provided in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-305 Instruction.
--------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-305(1): If an instruction has been originated by an appropriate person but is incomplete in any other respect, any person may complete it as authorized and the issuer may rely on it as completed, even though it has been completed incorrectly.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-305(2): 70A-8-107 Unless otherwise agreed, a person initiating an instruction assumes only the obligations imposed by Section


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-306 Effect of guaranteeing signature, indorsement, or instruction.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-306(1): A person who guarantees a signature of an indorser of a security certificate warrants that at the time of signing:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-306(1)(a): the signature was genuine;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-306(1)(b): the signer was an appropriate person to indorse, or if the signature is by an agent, the agent had actual authority to act on behalf of the appropriate person; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-306(1)(c): the signer had legal capacity to sign.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-306(2): A person who guarantees a signature of the originator of an instruction warrants that at the time of signing:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-306(2)(a): the signature was genuine;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-306(2)(b): the signer was an appropriate person to originate the instruction, or if the signature is by an agent, the agent had actual authority to act on behalf of the appropriate person, if the person specified in the instruction as the registered owner was, in fact, the registered owner, as to which fact the signature guarantor does not make a warranty; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-306(2)(c): the signer had legal capacity to sign.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-306(3): (2) A person who specially guarantees the signature of an originator of an instruction makes the warranties of a signature guarantor under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-306(3)(a): the person specified in the instruction as the registered owner of the uncertificated security will be the registered owner; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-306(3)(b): the transfer of the uncertificated security requested in the instruction will be registered by the issuer free from all liens, security interests, restrictions, and claims other than those specified in the instruction.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-306(4): (1); (2); (3) A guarantor under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-306(5): (1) A person who guarantees an indorsement of a security certificate makes the warranties of a signature guarantor under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-306(6): (3) A person who guarantees an instruction requesting the transfer of an uncertificated security makes the warranties of a special signature guarantor under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-306(7): An issuer may not require a special guaranty of signature, a guaranty of indorsement, or a guaranty of instruction as a condition to registration of transfer.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-306(8): The warranties under this section are made to a person taking or dealing with the security in reliance on the guaranty, and the guarantor is liable to the person for loss resulting from their breach.  An indorser or originator of an instruction whose signature, indorsement, or instruction has been guaranteed is liable to a guarantor for any loss suffered by the guarantor as a result of breach of the warranties of the guarantor.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-307 Purchaser's right to requisites for registration of transfer.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Unless otherwise agreed, the transferor of a security on due demand shall supply the purchaser with proof of authority to transfer or with any other requisite necessary to obtain registration of the transfer of the security, but if the transfer is not for value, a transferor need not comply unless the purchaser pays the necessary expenses.  If the transferor fails within a reasonable time to comply with the demand, the purchaser may reject or rescind the transfer.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-401 Duty of issuer to register transfer.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-401(1): 70A-8-402; 70A-8-204; 70A-8-403; 70A-8-403(2); 70A-8-403(4) If a certificated security in registered form is presented to an issuer with a request to register transfer or an instruction is presented to an issuer with a request to register transfer of an uncertificated security, the issuer shall register the transfer as requested if:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-401(1)(a): under the terms of the security the person seeking registration of transfer is eligible to have the security registered in its name;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-401(1)(b): the indorsement or instruction is made by the appropriate person or by an agent who has actual authority to act on behalf of the appropriate person;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-401(1)(c): 70A-8-402 reasonable assurance is given that the indorsement or instruction is genuine and authorized as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-401(1)(d): any applicable law relating to the collection of taxes has been complied with;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-401(1)(e): 70A-8-204 the transfer does not violate any restriction on transfer imposed by the issuer in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-401(1)(f): 70A-8-403; 70A-8-403(2); 70A-8-403(4) a demand that the issuer not register transfer has not become effective under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-401(1)(g): the transfer is in fact rightful or is to a protected purchaser.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-401(2): If an issuer is under a duty to register a transfer of a security, the issuer is liable to a person presenting a certificated security or an instruction for registration or to the person's principal for loss resulting from unreasonable delay in registration or failure or refusal to register the transfer.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-402 Assurance that indorsement or instruction is effective.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-402(1): 70A-8-106(1)(d); (1)(e) An issuer may require the following assurance that each necessary indorsement or each instruction is genuine and authorized:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-402(1)(a): in all cases, a guaranty of the signature of the person making an indorsement or originating an instruction including, in the case of an instruction, reasonable assurance of identity;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-402(1)(b): if the indorsement is made or the instruction is originated by an agent, appropriate assurance of actual authority to sign;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-402(1)(c): 70A-8-106(1)(d); (1)(e) if the indorsement is made or the instruction is originated by a fiduciary pursuant to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-402(1)(d): if there is more than one fiduciary, reasonable assurance that all who are required to sign have done so; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-402(1)(e): if the indorsement is made or the instruction is originated by a person not covered by another provision of this subsection, assurance appropriate to the case corresponding as nearly as may be to the provisions of this subsection.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-402(2): An issuer may elect to require reasonable assurance beyond that specified in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-402(3): In this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-402(3)(a): "Guaranty of the signature" means a guaranty signed by or on behalf of a person reasonably believed by the issuer to be responsible.  An issuer may adopt standards with respect to responsibility if they are not manifestly unreasonable.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-402(3)(b): "Appropriate evidence of appointment or incumbency" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-402(3)(b)(i): in the case of a fiduciary appointed or qualified by a court, a certificate issued by or under the direction or supervision of the court or an officer thereof and dated within 60 days before the date of presentation for transfer; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-402(3)(b)(ii): in any other case, a copy of a document showing the appointment or a certificate issued by or on behalf of a person reasonably believed by an issuer to be responsible or, in the absence of that document or certificate, other evidence the issuer reasonably considers appropriate.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-403 Demand that issuer not register transfer.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-403(1): A person who is an appropriate person to make an indorsement or originate an instruction may demand that the issuer not register transfer of a security by communicating to the issuer a notification that identifies the registered owner and the issue of which the security is a part and provides an address for communications directed to the person making the demand.  The demand is effective only if it is received by the issuer at a time and in a manner affording the issuer reasonable opportunity to act on it.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-403(2): If a certificated security in registered form is presented to an issuer with a request to register transfer or an instruction is presented to an issuer with a request to register transfer of an uncertificated security after a demand that the issuer not register transfer has become effective, the issuer shall promptly communicate to:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-403(2)(a): the person who initiated the demand at the address provided in the demand; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-403(2)(b): the person who presented the security for registration of transfer or initiated the instruction requesting registration of transfer a notification stating that:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-403(2)(b)(i): the certificated security has been presented for registration of transfer or the instruction for registration of transfer of the uncertificated security has been received;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-403(2)(b)(ii): a demand that the issuer not register transfer had previously been received; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-403(2)(b)(iii): the issuer will withhold registration of transfer for a period of time stated in the notification in order to provide the person who initiated the demand an opportunity to obtain legal process or an indemnity bond.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-403(3): (2)(b)(iii) The period described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-403(4): An issuer is not liable to a person who initiated a demand that the issuer not register transfer for any loss the person suffers as a result of registration of a transfer pursuant to an effective indorsement or instruction if the person who initiated the demand does not, within the time stated in the issuer's communication, either:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-403(4)(a): obtain an appropriate restraining order, injunction, or other process from a court of competent jurisdiction enjoining the issuer from registering the transfer; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-403(4)(b): file with the issuer an indemnity bond, sufficient in the issuer's judgment to protect the issuer and any transfer agent, registrar, or other agent of the issuer involved from any loss it or they may suffer by refusing to register the transfer.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-403(5): This section does not relieve an issuer from liability for registering transfer pursuant to an indorsement or instruction that was not effective.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-404 Wrongful registration.
------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-405 Replacement of lost, destroyed, or wrongfully taken security certificate.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-405(1): If an owner of a certificated security, whether in registered or bearer form, claims that the certificate has been lost, destroyed, or wrongfully taken, the issuer shall issue a new certificate if the owner:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-405(1)(a): requests that a new certificate be issued before the issuer has notice that the certificate has been acquired by a protected purchaser;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-405(1)(b): files with the issuer a sufficient indemnity bond; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-405(1)(c): satisfies other reasonable requirements imposed by the issuer.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-405(2): 70A-8-210
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-405(2)(a): If, after the issue of a new certificate, a protected purchaser of the original certificate presents it for registration of transfer, the issuer shall register the transfer unless an overissue would result.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-405(2)(b): 70A-8-210 If an overissue would result from registration of transfer, the issuer's liability is governed by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-405(2)(c): In addition to any rights on the indemnity bond, an issuer may recover the new certificate from a person to whom it was issued or any person taking under that person, except a protected purchaser.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-405(3): 70A-8-409.1 On and after July 1, 2011, this section does not apply to the replacement of a lost, destroyed, or wrongfully taken share certificate of a water company.  Section
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-405(4): 70A-8-409.1 On and after May 8, 2012, this section does not apply to the replacement of a lost, destroyed, or wrongfully taken share certificate of a land company.  Section


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-406 Obligation to notify issuer of lost, destroyed, or wrongfully taken security certificate.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-406(2): (1); 70A-8-409.1 On and after July 1, 2011, Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-407 Authenticating trustee, transfer agent, and registrar.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A person acting as authenticating trustee, transfer agent, registrar, or other agent for an issuer in the registration of a transfer of its securities, in the issue of new security certificates or uncertificated securities, or in the cancellation of surrendered security certificates has the same obligation to the holder or owner of a certificated or uncertificated security with regard to the particular functions performed as the issuer has in regard to those functions.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409 Application to land or water companies.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
The procedures of this chapter apply to shares of stock in a land company or a water company.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1 Replacement of lost, destroyed, or wrongfully taken share certificate of a land company or a water company.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(1): For purposes of this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(1)(a): "Affected share" means the share represented by a share certificate that is lost, destroyed, or wrongfully taken.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(1)(b): "Company" means a land company or a water company.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(1)(c): "Distribution area" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(1)(c)(i): for a water company, the geographic area where the water company distributes water; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(1)(c)(ii): for a land company, the geographic area owned by the land company.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(1)(d): "Original share certificate" means a share certificate that is alleged to be lost, destroyed, or wrongfully taken.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(1)(e): "Person" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(1)(e)(i): an individual;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(1)(e)(ii): a corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(1)(e)(iii): a business entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(1)(e)(iv): a political subdivision of the state, including a municipality;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(1)(e)(v): an agency of the state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(1)(e)(vi): an agency of the federal government.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(1)(f): "Replacement share certificate" means a share certificate issued to replace a share certificate that is lost, destroyed, or wrongfully taken.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(1)(g): "Share certificate" means a certificated share of stock in a company.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(2)(a): This section applies to the replacement of a lost, destroyed, or wrongfully taken share certificate.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(2)(b): Unless the articles of incorporation or bylaws of a company address the replacement of a lost, destroyed, or wrongfully taken share certificate, this section governs the replacement of a lost, destroyed, or wrongfully taken share certificate.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(3): (5) A company shall issue a replacement share certificate to a person claiming to be the owner of a share certificate that is lost, destroyed, or wrongfully taken, and cancel the original share certificate on the records of the company, if:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(3)(a): the person represents to the company that the original share certificate is lost, destroyed, or wrongfully taken;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(3)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(3)(b)(i): 
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(3)(b)(i)(A): the person is the registered owner of the affected share; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(3)(b)(i)(B): before the company receives notice that the share certificate has been acquired by a protected purchaser, the person requests that a replacement share certificate be issued; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(3)(b)(ii): 
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(3)(b)(ii)(A): the person is not the registered owner of the affected share; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(3)(b)(ii)(B): the person establishes ownership of the affected share, including by presenting to the company written documentation that demonstrates to the reasonable satisfaction of the company that the person is the rightful owner of the affected share through purchase, gift, inheritance, foreclosure, bankruptcy, or reorganization;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(3)(c): the assessments to which the affected share is subject are paid current;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(3)(d): (5) except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(3)(e): the person satisfies any other reasonable requirement imposed by the company, including the payment of a reasonable transfer fee.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(4): (5); (5)(d)
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(4)(a): If after a replacement share certificate is issued a protected purchaser of the original share certificate presents the original share certificate for registration of transfer, the company shall register the transfer unless an overissue would result.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(4)(b): If an overissue would result when there is a registration of transfer of an original share certificate, a company may recover the replacement share certificate from the person to whom it is issued, or any person taking under that person, except a protected purchaser.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(4)(c): (5); (5)(d) If a company elects to follow the procedures of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5): (3)(d); 16-6a-609; 45-1-101; (5)(a)(i)(A); (5)(a); (c); (5)(a)(i)(A); (5)(d); (5)(d); (5); (5); (5)(i); (5); (5); (5) As an alternative to requiring an indemnity bond or other acceptable security under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(a): 45-1-101; (5)(a)(i)(A) The company shall publish written notice at least once a week for three consecutive weeks:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(a)(i): 45-1-101
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(a)(i)(A): in a newspaper of general circulation in the area that reasonably includes the distribution area of the company; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(a)(i)(B): 45-1-101 as required in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(a)(ii): (5)(a)(i)(A) with at least seven days between each publication date under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(a)(iii): beginning no later than 20 days after submission of the request to issue the replacement share certificate.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(b): The company shall post written notice in at least three conspicuous places within the distribution area of the company.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(c): No later than 20 days after the day on which the company receives a request to issue a replacement share certificate, the company shall mail written notice:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(c)(i): to the last known address of the owner of the affected share shown on the records of the company;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(c)(ii): if a company maintains a record of who pays annual assessments, to any person who, within the five-year period immediately preceding the day the written notice is mailed, pays an assessment levied against the affected share; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(c)(iii): to any person that has notified the company in writing of an interest in the affected share, including a financial institution.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(d): (5)(a); (c); (5)(a)(i)(A) A notice required under Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(d)(i): identify the person who is requesting that a replacement share certificate be issued;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(d)(ii): state that an interested person may file a written notice of objection with the company; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(d)(iii): (5)(a)(i)(A) state that unless a written notice of objection to the issuance of a replacement share certificate is filed within 60 days after the last day of publication under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(d)(iii)(A): a replacement share certificate will be issued to the person requesting that the replacement share certificate be issued; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(d)(iii)(B): the original share certificate will be permanently canceled on the records of the company.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(e): (5)(d) A notice of objection under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(e)(i): state the basis for objecting to the claim of ownership of the affected share;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(e)(ii): identify a person that the objecting person believes has a stronger claim of ownership to the affected share; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(e)(iii): be accompanied by written evidence that reasonably documents the basis of the objection to the claim of ownership.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(f): (5)(d) If the company receives a notice of objection within the 60-day period described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(f)(i): deny in writing the objection to the claim of ownership and issue a replacement share certificate to the person requesting the replacement share certificate;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(f)(ii): accept in writing a claim of ownership asserted by a notice of objection and issue a replacement share certificate to the person the objecting person asserts owns the affected share;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(f)(iii): file an interpleader action in accordance with Utah Rules of Civil Procedure, Rule 22, joining the persons claiming an interest in the affected share and depositing a replacement share certificate with the court; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(f)(iv): require the persons claiming an interest in the affected share to resolve the ownership dispute.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(g): Upon receipt, the company shall act in accordance with:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(g)(i): a written agreement acceptable to the company among the persons who claim interest in the affected share; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(g)(ii): a court order declaring ownership in the affected share.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(h): (5) The following are entitled to receive from a nonprevailing person the costs for resolution of a dispute under this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(h)(i): a prevailing person; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(h)(ii): the company, if the company acts in good faith.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(i): (5); (5)(i) The person requesting that a replacement share certificate be issued shall reimburse the company for the costs reasonably incurred by the company under this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(i)(i): legal and other professional fees; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(i)(ii): costs incurred by the company in response to a notice of objection.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(j): (5); (5) A company shall comply with this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(j)(i): upon request from the person requesting a replacement share certificate be issued; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(j)(ii): (5) if the person requesting the replacement share certificate provides indemnification satisfactory to the company against liability and costs of proceeding under this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(5)(k): (5) A determination made under this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(6): (5); (6)(a); (6)(b); (6)(a); (6); (6)(d)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(6)(a): (5) A company shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(6)(a)(i): make a decision to approve or deny the issuance of a replacement share certificate in writing; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(6)(a)(ii): (5) deliver the written decision to:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(6)(a)(ii)(A): the person requesting a replacement share certificate be issued;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(6)(a)(ii)(B): (5) a person who files a notice of objection under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(6)(a)(ii)(C): any other person the company determines is involved in the request for a replacement share certificate.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(6)(b): (6)(a) A decision of a company described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(6)(c): (6)(b); (6)(a) A person may not seek judicial review under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(6)(d): (6); (6)(d)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(6)(d)(i): (6) In a judicial action brought under this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(6)(d)(i)(A): the costs of successfully defending its ownership claim; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(6)(d)(i)(B): reasonable attorney fees.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-409.1(6)(d)(ii): (6)(d)(i) Notwithstanding Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-501 Securities account -- Acquisition of security entitlement from securities intermediary.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-501(1): "Securities account" means an account to which a financial asset is or may be credited in accordance with an agreement under which the person maintaining the account undertakes to treat the person for whom the account is maintained as entitled to exercise the rights that comprise the financial asset.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-501(2): (4); (5) Except as otherwise provided in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-501(2)(a): indicates by book entry that a financial asset has been credited to the person's securities account;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-501(2)(b): receives a financial asset from the person or acquires a financial asset for the person and, in either case, accepts it for credit to the person's securities account; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-501(2)(c): becomes obligated under other law, regulation, or rule to credit a financial asset to the person's securities account.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-501(3): (2) If a condition of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-501(4): If a securities intermediary holds a financial asset for another person, and the financial asset is registered in the name of, payable to the order of, or specially indorsed to the other person, and has not been indorsed to the securities intermediary or in blank, the other person is treated as holding the financial asset directly rather than as having a security entitlement with respect to the financial asset.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-501(5): Issuance of a security is not establishment of a security entitlement.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-502 Assertion of adverse claim against entitlement holder.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
An action based on an adverse claim to a financial asset, whether framed in conversion, replevin, constructive trust, equitable lien, or other theory, may not be asserted against a person who acquires a security entitlement under Section

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-503(4)(a)(i): insolvency proceedings have been initiated by or against the securities intermediary;

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-503(4)(a)(iii): 70A-8-504 the securities intermediary violated its obligations under Section

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-504 Duty of securities intermediary to maintain financial asset.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-504(1): A securities intermediary shall promptly obtain and thereafter maintain a financial asset in a quantity corresponding to the aggregate of all security entitlements it has established in favor of its entitlement holders with respect to that financial asset.  The securities intermediary may maintain those financial assets directly or through one or more other securities intermediaries.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-504(2): (1) Except to the extent otherwise agreed by its entitlement holder, a securities intermediary may not grant any security interests in a financial asset it is obligated to maintain pursuant to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-504(3): (1) A securities intermediary satisfies the duty in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-504(3)(a): the securities intermediary acts with respect to the duty as agreed upon by the entitlement holder and the securities intermediary; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-504(3)(b): in the absence of agreement, the securities intermediary exercises due care in accordance with reasonable commercial standards to obtain and maintain the financial asset.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-504(4): This section does not apply to a clearing corporation that is itself the obligor of an option or similar obligation to which its entitlement holders have security entitlements.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-505 Duty of securities intermediary with respect to payments and distributions.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-505(1): A securities intermediary shall take action to obtain a payment or distribution made by the issuer of a financial asset.  A securities intermediary satisfies the duty if:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-505(1)(a): the securities intermediary acts with respect to the duty as agreed upon by the entitlement holder and the securities intermediary; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-505(1)(b): in the absence of agreement, the securities intermediary exercises due care in accordance with reasonable commercial standards to attempt to obtain the payment or distribution.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-505(2): A securities intermediary is obligated to its entitlement holder for a payment or distribution made by the issuer of a financial asset if the payment or distribution is received by the securities intermediary.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-506 Duty of securities intermediary to exercise rights as directed by entitlement holder.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A securities intermediary shall exercise rights with respect to a financial asset if directed to do so by an entitlement holder.  A securities intermediary satisfies the duty if:Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-506(1): the securities intermediary acts with respect to the duty as agreed upon by the entitlement holder and the securities intermediary; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-506(2): in the absence of agreement, the securities intermediary either places the entitlement holder in a position to exercise the rights directly or exercises due care in accordance with reasonable commercial standards to follow the direction of the entitlement holder.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-507 Duty of securities intermediary to comply with entitlement order.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-507(1): A securities intermediary shall comply with an entitlement order if the entitlement order is originated by the appropriate person, the securities intermediary has had reasonable opportunity to assure itself that the entitlement order is genuine and authorized, and the securities intermediary has had reasonable opportunity to comply with the entitlement order.  A securities intermediary satisfies the duty if:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-507(1)(a): the securities intermediary acts with respect to the duty as agreed upon by the entitlement holder and the securities intermediary; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-507(1)(b): in the absence of agreement, the securities intermediary exercises due care in accordance with reasonable commercial standards to comply with the entitlement order.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-507(2): If a securities intermediary transfers a financial asset pursuant to an ineffective entitlement order, the securities intermediary shall reestablish a security entitlement in favor of the person entitled to it, and pay or credit any payments or distributions that the person did not receive as a result of the wrongful transfer.  If the securities intermediary does not reestablish a security entitlement, the securities intermediary is liable to the entitlement holder for damages.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-508 Duty of securities intermediary to change entitlement holder's position to other form of security holding.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A securities intermediary shall act at the direction of an entitlement holder to change a security entitlement into another available form of holding for which the entitlement holder is eligible, or to cause the financial asset to be transferred to a securities account of the entitlement holder with another securities intermediary.  A securities intermediary satisfies the duty if:Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-508(1): the securities intermediary acts as agreed upon by the entitlement holder and the securities intermediary; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-508(2): in the absence of agreement, the securities intermediary exercises due care in accordance with reasonable commercial standards to follow the direction of the entitlement holder.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-509 Specification of duties of securities intermediary by other statute or regulation -- Manner of performance of duties of securities intermediary and exercise of rights of entitlement holder.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-509(1): 70A-8-504; 70A-8-508 If the substance of a duty imposed upon a securities intermediary by Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-509(2): To the extent that specific standards for the performance of the duties of a securities intermediary or the exercise of the rights of an entitlement holder are not specified by other statute, regulation, or rule or by agreement between the securities intermediary and entitlement holder, the securities intermediary shall perform its duties and the entitlement holder shall exercise its rights in a commercially reasonable manner.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-509(3): 70A-8-504; 70A-8-508 The obligation of a securities intermediary to perform the duties imposed by Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-509(3)(a): rights of the securities intermediary arising out of a security interest under a security agreement with the entitlement holder or otherwise; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-509(3)(b): rights of the securities intermediary under other law, regulation, rule, or agreement to withhold performance of its duties as a result of unfulfilled obligations of the entitlement holder to the securities intermediary.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-509(4): 70A-8-504; 70A-8-508 Sections

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-510(1): Chapter 9a, Uniform Commercial Code - Secured Transactions; (3) In a case not covered by the priority rules in

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-511 Priority among security interests and entitlement holders.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-511(1): (2); (3) Except as otherwise provided in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-511(2): A claim of a creditor of a securities intermediary who has a security interest in a financial asset held by a securities intermediary has priority over claims of the securities intermediary's entitlement holders who have security entitlements with respect to that financial asset if the creditor has control over the financial asset.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-511(3): If a clearing corporation does not have sufficient financial assets to satisfy both its obligations to entitlement holders who have security entitlements with respect to a financial asset and its obligation to a creditor of the clearing corporation who has a security interest in that financial asset, the claim of the creditor has priority over the claims of entitlement holders.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-601 Transition provisions.
------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-601(1): This act does not affect an action or proceeding commenced before this act takes effect.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-8-601(2): If a security interest in a security is perfected at the date this act takes effect, and the action by which the security interest was perfected would suffice to perfect a security interest under this act, no further action is required to continue perfection.  If a security interest in a security is perfected at the date this act takes effect but the action by which the security interest was perfected would not suffice to perfect a security interest under this act, the security interest remains perfected for a period of four months after the effective date and continues perfected thereafter if appropriate action to perfect under this act is taken within that period.  If a security interest is perfected at the date this act takes effect and the security interest can be perfected by filing under this act, a financing statement signed by the secured party instead of the debtor may be filed within that period to continue perfection or thereafter to perfect.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 70A - Chapter 9a - Uniform Commercial Code - Secured Transactions
*********************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-101 Title.
---------------------------------------
This chapter may be cited as Uniform Commercial Code - Secured Transactions.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102 Definitions and index of definitions.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
In this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(1): "Accession" means goods that are physically united with other goods in such a manner that the identity of the original goods is not lost.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(2)(a): "Account," except as used in "account for," means a right to payment of a monetary obligation, whether or not earned by performance:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(2)(a)(i): for property that has been or is to be sold, leased, licensed, assigned, or otherwise disposed of;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(2)(a)(ii): for services rendered or to be rendered;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(2)(a)(iii): for a policy of insurance issued or to be issued;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(2)(a)(iv): for a secondary obligation incurred or to be incurred;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(2)(a)(v): for energy provided or to be provided;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(2)(a)(vi): for the use or hire of a vessel under a charter or other contract;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(2)(a)(vii): arising out of the use of a credit or charge card or information contained on or for use with the card; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(2)(a)(viii): as winnings in a lottery or other game of chance operated or sponsored by a state, governmental unit of a state, or person licensed or authorized to operate the game by a state or governmental unit of a state.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(2)(b): "Account" includes health-care-insurance receivables.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(2)(c): "Account" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(2)(c)(i): rights to payment evidenced by chattel paper or an instrument;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(2)(c)(ii): commercial tort claims;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(2)(c)(iii): deposit accounts;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(2)(c)(iv): investment property;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(2)(c)(v): letter-of-credit rights or letters of credit; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(2)(c)(vi): rights to payment for money or funds advanced or sold, other than rights arising out of the use of a credit or charge card or information contained on or for use with the card.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(3)(a): "Account debtor" means a person obligated on an account, chattel paper, or general intangible.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(3)(b): "Account debtor" does not include persons obligated to pay a negotiable instrument, even if the instrument constitutes part of chattel paper.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(4): "Accounting," except as used in "accounting for," means a record:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(4)(a): authenticated by a secured party;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(4)(b): indicating the aggregate unpaid secured obligations as of a date not more than 35 days earlier or 35 days later than the date of the record; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(4)(c): identifying the components of the obligations in reasonable detail.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(5): "Agricultural lien" means an interest, other than a security interest, in farm products:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(5)(a): which secures payment or performance of an obligation for:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(5)(a)(i): goods or services furnished in connection with a debtor's farming operation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(5)(a)(ii): rent on real property leased by a debtor in connection with its farming operation;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(5)(b): which is created by statute in favor of a person that:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(5)(b)(i): in the ordinary course of its business furnished goods or services to a debtor in connection with a debtor's farming operation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(5)(b)(ii): leased real property to a debtor in connection with the debtor's farming operation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(5)(c): whose effectiveness does not depend on the person's possession of the personal property.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(6): "As-extracted collateral" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(6)(a): oil, gas, or other minerals that are subject to a security interest that:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(6)(a)(i): is created by a debtor having an interest in the minerals before extraction; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(6)(a)(ii): attaches to the minerals as extracted; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(6)(b): accounts arising out of the sale at the wellhead or minehead of oil, gas, or other minerals in which the debtor had an interest before extraction.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(7): "Authenticate" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(7)(a): to sign; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(7)(b): with present intent to adopt or accept a record, to attach to or logically associate with the record an electronic sound, symbol, or process.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(8): 7-1-103
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(8)(a): "Bank" means an organization that is engaged in the business of banking.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(8)(b): 7-1-103 "Bank" includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(8)(b)(i): 7-1-103 a depository institution as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(8)(b)(ii): a trust company.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(9): "Cash proceeds" means proceeds that are money, checks, deposit accounts, or the like.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(10): 
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(10)(a): "Certificate of title" means a certificate of title with respect to which a statute provides for the security interest in question to be indicated on the certificate as a condition or result of the security interest's obtaining priority over the rights of a lien creditor with respect to the collateral.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(10)(b): "Certificate of title" includes another record maintained as an alternative to a certificate of title by the governmental unit that issues certificates of title if a statute permits the security interest in question to be indicated on the record as a condition or result of the security interest's obtaining priority over the rights of a lien creditor with respect to the collateral.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(11): (11)
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(11)(a): (11) "Chattel paper" means a record or records that evidence both a monetary obligation and a security interest in specific goods, a security interest in specific goods and software used in the goods, a security interest in specific goods and license of software used in the goods, a lease of specific goods, or a lease of specific goods and license of software used in the goods.  In this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(11)(b): "Chattel paper" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(11)(b)(i): charters or other contracts involving the use or hire of a vessel; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(11)(b)(ii): records that evidence a right to payment arising out of the use of a credit or charge card or information contained or for use with the card.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(11)(c): If a transaction is evidenced by records that include an instrument or series of instruments, the group of records taken together constitutes chattel paper.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(12): "Collateral" means the property subject to a security interest or agricultural lien.  "Collateral" includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(12)(a): proceeds to which a security interest attaches;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(12)(b): accounts, chattel paper, payment intangibles, and promissory notes that have been sold; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(12)(c): goods that are the subject of a consignment.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(13): "Commercial tort claim" means a claim arising in tort with respect to which:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(13)(a): the claimant is an organization; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(13)(b): the claimant is an individual and the claim:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(13)(b)(i): arose in the course of the claimant's business or profession; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(13)(b)(ii): does not include damages arising out of personal injury to or the death of an individual.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(14): "Commodity account" means an account maintained by a commodity intermediary in which a commodity contract is carried for a commodity customer.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(15): "Commodity contract" means a commodity futures contract, an option on a commodity futures contract, a commodity option, or another contract if the contract or option is:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(15)(a): traded on or subject to the rules of a board of trade that has been designated as a contract market for such a contract pursuant to federal commodities laws; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(15)(b): traded on a foreign commodity board of trade, exchange, or market, and is carried on the books of a commodity intermediary for a commodity customer.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(16): "Commodity customer" means a person for which a commodity intermediary carries a commodity contract on its books.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(17): "Commodity intermediary" means a person that:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(17)(a): is registered as a futures commission merchant under federal commodities law; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(17)(b): in the ordinary course of its business provides clearance or settlement services for a board of trade that has been designated as a contract market pursuant to federal commodities law.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(18): "Communicate" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(18)(a): to send a written or other tangible record;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(18)(b): to transmit a record by any means agreed upon by the persons sending and receiving the record; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(18)(c): in the case of transmission of a record to or by a filing office, to transmit a record by any means prescribed by filing-office rule.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(19): "Consignee" means a merchant to which goods are delivered in a consignment.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(20): "Consignment" means a transaction, regardless of its form, in which a person delivers goods to a merchant for the purpose of sale and:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(20)(a): the merchant:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(20)(a)(i): deals in goods of that kind under a name other than the name of the person making delivery;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(20)(a)(ii): is not an auctioneer; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(20)(a)(iii): is not generally known by its creditors to be substantially engaged in selling the goods of others;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(20)(b): with respect to each delivery, the aggregate value of the goods is $1,000 or more at the time of delivery;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(20)(c): the goods are not consumer goods immediately before delivery; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(20)(d): the transaction does not create a security interest that secures an obligation.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(21): "Consignor" means a person that delivers goods to a consignee in a consignment.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(22): "Consumer debtor" means a debtor in a consumer transaction.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(23): "Consumer goods" means goods that are used or bought for use primarily for personal, family, or household purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(24): "Consumer-goods transaction" means a consumer transaction in which:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(24)(a): an individual incurs an obligation primarily for personal, family, or household purposes; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(24)(b): a security interest in consumer goods secures the obligation.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(25): "Consumer obligor" means an obligor who is an individual and who incurred the obligation as part of a transaction entered into primarily for personal, family, or household purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(26): 
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(26)(a): "Consumer transaction" means a transaction in which:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(26)(a)(i): an individual incurs an obligation primarily for personal, family, or household purposes;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(26)(a)(ii): a security interest secures the obligation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(26)(a)(iii): the collateral is held or acquired primarily for personal, family, or household purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(26)(b): "Consumer transaction" includes consumer-goods transactions.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(27): "Continuation statement" means an amendment of a financing statement which:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(27)(a): identifies, by its file number, the initial financing statement to which it relates; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(27)(b): indicates that it is a continuation statement for, or that it is filed to continue the effectiveness of, the identified financing statement.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(28): "Debtor" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(28)(a): a person having an interest, other than a security interest or other lien, in the collateral, whether or not the person is an obligor;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(28)(b): a seller of accounts, chattel paper, payment intangibles, or promissory notes; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(28)(c): a consignee.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(29): 
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(29)(a): "Deposit account" means a demand, time, savings, passbook, or similar account maintained with a bank.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(29)(b): "Deposit account" does not include investment property or accounts evidenced by an instrument.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(30): 70A-7a-201(2) "Document" means a document of title or a receipt of the type described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(31): "Electronic chattel paper" means chattel paper evidenced by a record or records consisting of information stored in an electronic medium.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(32): "Encumbrance" means a right, other than an ownership interest, in real property.  "Encumbrance" includes mortgages and other liens on real property.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(33): "Equipment" means goods other than inventory, farm products, or consumer goods.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(34): "Farm products" means goods, other than standing timber, with respect to which the debtor is engaged in a farming operation and which are:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(34)(a): crops grown, growing, or to be grown, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(34)(a)(i): crops produced on trees, vines, and bushes; and

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(34)(d): products of crops or livestock in their unmanufactured states.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(35): "Farming operation" means raising, cultivating, propagating, fattening, grazing, or any other farming, livestock, or aquacultural operation.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(36): 70A-9a-519(1) "File number" means the number assigned to an initial financing statement pursuant to Subsection
