Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(40): 70A-9a-502(1); (2)
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(40)(a): 70A-9a-502(1); (2) "Fixture filing" means the filing of a financing statement covering goods that are or are to become fixtures and satisfying Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(40)(b): "Fixture filing" includes the filing of a financing statement covering goods of a transmitting utility which are or are to become fixtures.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(41): "Fixtures" means goods that have become so related to particular real property that an interest in them arises under real property law.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(42): 
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(42)(a): "General intangible" means any personal property, including things in action, other than accounts, chattel paper, commercial tort claims, deposit accounts, documents, goods, instruments, investment property, letter-of-credit rights, letters of credit, money, and oil, gas, or other minerals before extraction.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(42)(b): "General intangible" includes payment intangibles and software.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(43): "Good faith" means honesty in fact and the observance of reasonable commercial standards of fair dealing.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(44): 
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(44)(a): "Goods" means all things that are movable when a security interest attaches.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(44)(b): "Goods" includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(44)(b)(i): fixtures;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(44)(b)(ii): standing timber that is to be cut and removed under a conveyance or contract for sale;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(44)(b)(iii): the unborn young of animals;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(44)(b)(iv): crops grown, growing, or to be grown, even if the crops are produced on trees, vines, or bushes; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(44)(b)(v): manufactured homes.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(44)(c): "Goods" also includes a computer program embedded in goods and any supporting information provided in connection with a transaction relating to the program if:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(44)(c)(i): the program is associated with the goods in such a manner that it customarily is considered part of the goods; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(44)(c)(ii): by becoming the owner of the goods, a person acquires a right to use the program in connection with the goods.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(44)(d): "Goods" does not include a computer program embedded in goods that consist solely of the medium in which the program is embedded.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(44)(e): "Goods" also does not include accounts, chattel paper, commercial tort claims, deposit accounts, documents, general intangibles, instruments, investment property, letter-of-credit rights, letters of credit, money, or oil, gas, or other minerals before extraction.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(45): 
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(45)(a): "Governmental unit" means a subdivision, agency, department, county, parish, municipality, or other unit of the government of the United States, a state, or a foreign country.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(45)(b): "Governmental unit" includes an organization having a separate corporate existence if the organization is eligible to issue debt on which interest is exempt from income taxation under the laws of the United States.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(46): "Health-care-insurance receivable" means an interest in or claim under a policy of insurance which is a right to payment of a monetary obligation for health-care goods or services provided.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(47): 
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(47)(a): "Instrument" means a negotiable instrument or any other writing that evidences a right to the payment of a monetary obligation, is not itself a security agreement or lease, and is of a type that in ordinary course of business is transferred by delivery with any necessary indorsement or assignment.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(47)(b): "Instrument" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(47)(b)(i): investment property;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(47)(b)(ii): letters of credit; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(47)(b)(iii): writings that evidence a right to payment arising out of the use of a credit or charge card or information contained on or for use with the card.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(48): "Inventory" means goods, other than farm products, which:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(48)(a): are leased by a person as lessor;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(48)(b): are held by a person for sale or lease or to be furnished under a contract of service;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(48)(c): are furnished by a person under a contract of service; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(48)(d): consist of raw materials, work in process, or materials used or consumed in a business.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(49): "Investment property" means a security, whether certificated or uncertificated, security entitlement, securities account, commodity contract, or commodity account.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(50): "Jurisdiction of organization," with respect to a registered organization, means the jurisdiction under whose law the organization is formed or organized.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(51): 
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(51)(a): "Letter-of-credit right" means a right to payment or performance under a letter of credit, whether or not the beneficiary has demanded or is at the time entitled to demand payment or performance.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(51)(b): "Letter-of-credit right" does not include the right of a beneficiary to demand payment or performance under a letter of credit.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(52): "Lien creditor" means:

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(65): "Promissory note" means an instrument that evidences a promise to pay a monetary obligation, does not evidence an order to pay, and does not contain an acknowledgment by a bank that the bank has received for deposit a sum of money or funds.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(70): "Record," except as used in "for record," "of record," "record or legal title," and "record owner," means information that is inscribed on a tangible medium or which is stored in an electronic or other medium and is retrievable in perceivable form.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(80)(b): indicates either that it is a termination statement or that the identified financing statement is no longer effective.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-102(81)(d): transmitting or producing and transmitting electricity, steam, gas, or water.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-103 Purchase-money security interest -- Application of payments -- Burden of establishing.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-103(1): In this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-103(1)(a): "purchase-money collateral" means goods or software that secures a purchase-money obligation incurred with respect to that collateral; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-103(1)(b): "purchase-money obligation" means an obligation of an obligor incurred as all or part of the price of the collateral or for value given to enable the debtor to acquire rights in or the use of the collateral if the value is in fact so used.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-103(2): A security interest in goods is a purchase-money security interest:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-103(2)(a): to the extent that the goods are purchase-money collateral with respect to that security interest;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-103(2)(b): if the security interest is in inventory that is or was purchase-money collateral, also to the extent that the security interest secures a purchase-money obligation incurred with respect to other inventory in which the secured party holds or held a purchase-money security interest; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-103(2)(c): also to the extent that the security interest secures a purchase-money obligation incurred with respect to software in which the secured party holds or held a purchase-money security interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-103(3): A security interest in software is a purchase-money security interest to the extent that the security interest also secures a purchase-money obligation incurred with respect to goods in which the secured party holds or held a purchase-money security interest if:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-103(3)(a): the debtor acquired its interest in the software in an integrated transaction in which it acquired an interest in the goods; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-103(3)(b): the debtor acquired its interest in the software for the principal purpose of using the software in the goods.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-103(4): The security interest of a consignor in goods that are the subject of a consignment is a purchase-money security interest in inventory.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-103(5): In a transaction other than a consumer-goods transaction, if the extent to which a security interest is a purchase-money security interest depends on the application of a payment to a particular obligation, the payment must be applied:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-103(5)(a): in accordance with any reasonable method of application to which the parties agree;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-103(5)(b): in the absence of the parties' agreement to a reasonable method, in accordance with any intention of the obligor manifested at or before the time of payment; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-103(5)(c): in the absence of an agreement to a reasonable method and a timely manifestation of the obligor's intention, in the following order:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-103(5)(c)(i): to obligations that are not secured; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-103(5)(c)(ii): if more than one obligation is secured, to obligations secured by purchase-money security interests in the order in which those obligations were incurred.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-103(6): In a transaction other than a consumer-goods transaction, a purchase-money security interest does not lose its status as such, even if:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-103(6)(a): the purchase-money collateral also secures an obligation that is not a purchase-money obligation;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-103(6)(b): collateral that is not purchase-money collateral also secures the purchase-money obligation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-103(6)(c): the purchase-money obligation has been renewed, refinanced, consolidated, or restructured.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-103(7): In a transaction other than a consumer-goods transaction, a secured party claiming a purchase-money security interest has the burden of establishing the extent to which the security interest is a purchase-money security interest.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-105 Control of electronic chattel paper.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-105(1): A secured party has control of electronic chattel paper if a system employed by evidencing the transfer of interests in the chattel paper reliably establishes the secured party as the person to whom the chattel paper was assigned.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-105(2): (1); (2)(d); (e); (f) A system satisfies Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-105(2)(a): (2)(d); (e); (f) a single authoritative copy of the record or records exists which is unique, identifiable and, except as otherwise provided in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-105(2)(b): the authoritative copy identifies the secured party as the assignee of the record or records;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-105(2)(c): the authoritative copy is communicated to and maintained by the secured party or its designated custodian;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-105(2)(d): copies or amendments that add or change an identified assignee of the authoritative copy can be made only with the consent of the secured party;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-105(2)(e): each copy of the authoritative copy and any copy of a copy is readily identifiable as a copy that is not the authoritative copy; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-105(2)(f): any amendment of the authoritative copy is readily identifiable as authorized or unauthorized.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-106 Control of investment property.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-106(2): A secured party has control of a commodity contract if:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-106(2)(a): the secured party is the commodity intermediary with which the commodity contract is carried; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-106(2)(b): the commodity customer, secured party, and commodity intermediary have agreed that the commodity intermediary will apply any value distributed on account of the commodity contract as directed by the secured party without further consent by the commodity customer.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-106(3): A secured party having control of all security entitlements or commodity contracts carried in a securities account or commodity account has control over the securities account or commodity account.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-202 Title to collateral immaterial.
----------------------------------------------------------------
Except as otherwise provided with respect to consignments or sales of accounts, chattel paper, payment intangibles, or promissory notes, the provisions of this chapter with regard to rights and obligations apply whether title to collateral is in the secured party or the debtor.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-205 Use or disposition of collateral permissible.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-205(1)(a): the debtor has the right or ability to:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-205(1)(a)(i): use, commingle, or dispose of all or part of the collateral, including returned or repossessed goods;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-205(1)(a)(ii): collect, compromise, enforce, or otherwise deal with collateral;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-205(1)(a)(iii): accept the return of collateral or make repossessions; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-205(1)(a)(iv): use, commingle, or dispose of proceeds; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-205(1)(b): the secured party fails to require the debtor to account for proceeds or replace collateral.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-205(2): This section does not relax the requirements of possession if attachment, perfection, or enforcement of a security interest depends upon possession of the collateral by the secured party.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-210 Request for accounting -- Request regarding list of collateral or statement of account.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-210(1): (1)(b); (c); (d) In this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-210(1)(a): (1)(b); (c); (d) "Request" means a record of a type described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-210(1)(b): "Request for an accounting" means a record authenticated by a debtor requesting that the recipient provide an accounting of the unpaid obligations secured by collateral and reasonably identifying the transaction or relationship that is the subject of the request.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-210(1)(c): "Request regarding a list of collateral" means a record authenticated by a debtor requesting that the recipient approve or correct a list of what the debtor believes to be the collateral securing an obligation and reasonably identifying the transaction or relationship that is the subject of the request.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-210(1)(d): "Request regarding a statement of account" means a record authenticated by a debtor requesting that the recipient approve or correct a statement indicating what the debtor believes to be the aggregate amount of unpaid obligations secured by collateral as of a specified date and reasonably identifying the transaction or relationship that is the subject of the request.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-210(2): (3); (4); (5); (6) Subject to Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-210(2)(a): in the case of a request for an accounting, by authenticating and sending to the debtor an accounting; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-210(2)(b): in the case of a request regarding a list of collateral or a request regarding a statement of account, by authenticating and sending to the debtor an approval or correction.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-210(3): A secured party that claims a security interest in all of a particular type of collateral owned by the debtor may comply with a request regarding a list of collateral by sending to the debtor an authenticated record including a statement to that effect within 14 days after receipt.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-210(4): A person that receives a request regarding a list of collateral, claims no interest in the collateral when it receives the request, and claimed an interest in the collateral at an earlier time shall comply with the request within 14 days after receipt by sending to the debtor an authenticated record:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-210(4)(a): disclaiming any interest in the collateral; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-210(4)(b): if known to the recipient, providing the name and mailing address of any assignee of or successor to the recipient's interest in the collateral.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-210(5): A person that receives a request for an accounting or a request regarding a statement of account, claims no interest in the obligations when it receives the request, and claimed an interest in the obligations at an earlier time shall comply with the request within 14 days after receipt by sending to the debtor an authenticated record:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-210(5)(a): disclaiming any interest in the obligations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-210(5)(b): if known to the recipient, providing the name and mailing address of any assignee of or successor to the recipient's interest in the obligations.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-210(6): A debtor is entitled without charge to one response to a request under this section during any six-month period.  The secured party may require payment of a charge not exceeding $25 for each additional response.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-301 Law governing perfection and priority of security interests.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Except as otherwise provided in SectionsUtah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-301(1): Except as otherwise provided in this section, while a debtor is located in a jurisdiction, the local law of that jurisdiction governs perfection, the effect of perfection or nonperfection, and the priority of a security interest in collateral.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-301(2): While collateral is located in a jurisdiction, the local law of that jurisdiction governs perfection, the effect of perfection or nonperfection, and the priority of a possessory security interest in that collateral.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-301(3): (4) Except as otherwise provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-301(3)(a): perfection of a security interest in the goods by filing a fixture filing;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-301(3)(b): perfection of a security interest in timber to be cut; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-301(3)(c): the effect of perfection or nonperfection and the priority of a nonpossessory security interest in the collateral.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-301(4): The local law of the jurisdiction in which the wellhead or minehead is located governs perfection, the effect of perfection or nonperfection, and the priority of a security interest in as-extracted collateral.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-302 Law governing perfection and priority of agricultural liens.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
While farm products are located in a jurisdiction, the local law of that jurisdiction governs perfection, the effect of perfection or nonperfection, and the priority of an agricultural lien on the farm products.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-303 Law governing perfection and priority of security interests in goods covered by a certificate of title.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-303(1): This section applies to goods covered by a certificate of title, even if there is no other relationship between the jurisdiction under whose certificate of title the goods are covered and the goods or the debtor.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-303(2): Goods become covered by a certificate of title when a valid application for the certificate of title and the applicable fee are delivered to the appropriate authority.  Goods cease to be covered by a certificate of title at the earlier of the time the certificate of title ceases to be effective under the law of the issuing jurisdiction or the time the goods become covered subsequently by a certificate of title issued by another jurisdiction.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-303(3): The local law of the jurisdiction under whose certificate of title the goods are covered governs perfection, the effect of perfection or nonperfection, and the priority of a security interest in goods covered by a certificate of title from the time the goods become covered by the certificate of title until the goods cease to be covered by the certificate of title.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-304 Law governing perfection and priority of security interests in deposit accounts.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-304(1): The local law of a bank's jurisdiction governs perfection, the effect of perfection or nonperfection, and the priority of a security interest in a deposit account maintained with that bank.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-304(2): (2)(a); (2)(a); (2)(b) The following rules determine a bank's jurisdiction for purposes of this part:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-304(2)(a): If an agreement between the bank and the debtor governing the deposit account expressly provides that a particular jurisdiction is the bank's jurisdiction for purposes of this part, this chapter, or this title, that jurisdiction is the bank's jurisdiction.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-304(2)(b): (2)(a) If Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-304(2)(c): (2)(a); (2)(b) If neither Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-304(2)(d): If none of the preceding subsections applies, the bank's jurisdiction is the jurisdiction in which the office identified in an account statement as the office serving the customer's account is located.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-304(2)(e): If none of the preceding subsections applies, the bank's jurisdiction is the jurisdiction in which the chief executive office of the bank is located.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-307 Location of debtor.
----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-307(1): In this section, "place of business" means a place where a debtor conducts its affairs.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-307(2): Except as otherwise provided in this section, the following rules determine a debtor's location:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-307(2)(a): A debtor who is an individual is located at the individual's principal residence.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-307(2)(b): A debtor that is an organization and has only one place of business is located at its place of business.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-307(2)(c): A debtor that is an organization and has more than one place of business is located at its chief executive office.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-307(3): (2); (2) Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-307(4): (2); (3) A person that ceases to exist, have a residence, or have a place of business continues to be located in the jurisdiction specified by Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-307(5): A registered organization that is organized under the law of a state is located in that state.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-307(6): (9); (6)(a); (6)(b) Except as otherwise provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-307(6)(a): in the state that the law of the United States designates, if the law designates a state of location;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-307(6)(b): in the state that the registered organization, branch, or agency designates, if the law of the United States authorizes the registered organization, branch, or agency to designate its state of location, including by designating its main office, home office, or other comparable office; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-307(6)(c): (6)(a); (6)(b) in the District of Columbia, if neither Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-307(7): (5); (6) A registered organization continues to be located in the jurisdiction specified by Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-307(7)(a): the suspension, revocation, forfeiture, or lapse of the registered organization's status as such in its jurisdiction of organization; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-307(7)(b): the dissolution, winding up, or cancellation of the existence of the registered organization.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-307(8): The United States is located in the District of Columbia.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-307(9): A branch or agency of a bank that is not organized under the law of the United States or a state is located in the state in which the branch or agency is licensed, if all branches and agencies of the bank are licensed in only one state.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-307(10): A foreign air carrier under the Federal Aviation Act of 1958, as amended, is located at the designated office of the agent upon which service of process may be made on behalf of the carrier.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-307(11): This section applies only for purposes of this part.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-312(6)(b): loading, unloading, storing, shipping, transshipping, manufacturing, processing, or otherwise dealing with them in a manner preliminary to their sale or exchange.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-312(7)(b): presentation, collection, enforcement, renewal, or registration of transfer.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-318 No interest retained in right to payment that is sold -- Rights and title of seller of account or chattel paper with respect to creditors and purchasers.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-318(1): A debtor that has sold an account, chattel paper, payment intangible, or promissory note does not retain a legal or equitable interest in the collateral sold.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-318(2): For purposes of determining the rights of creditors of, and purchasers for value of an account or chattel paper from, a debtor that has sold an account or chattel paper, while the buyer's security interest is unperfected, the debtor is deemed to have rights and title to the account or chattel paper identical to those the debtor sold.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-321 Licensee of general intangible and lessee of goods in ordinary course of business.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-321(1): In this section, "licensee in ordinary course of business" means a person that becomes a licensee of a general intangible in good faith, without knowledge that the license violates the rights of another person in the general intangible, and in the ordinary course from a person in the business of licensing general intangibles of that kind.  A person becomes a licensee in the ordinary course if the license to the person comports with the usual or customary practices in the kind of business in which the licensor is engaged or with the licensor's own usual or customary practices.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-321(2): A licensee in ordinary course of business takes its rights under a nonexclusive license free of a security interest in the general intangible created by the licensor, even if the security interest is perfected and the licensee knows of its existence.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-321(3): A lessee in ordinary course of business takes its leasehold interest free of a security interest in the goods created by the lessor, even if the security interest is perfected and the lessee knows of its existence.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-322 Priorities among conflicting security interests in and agricultural liens on same collateral.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-322(1): Except as otherwise provided in this section, priority among conflicting security interests and agricultural liens in the same collateral is determined according to the following rules:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-322(1)(a): Conflicting perfected security interests and agricultural liens rank according to priority in time of filing or perfection.  Priority dates from the earlier of the time a filing covering the collateral is first made or the security interest or agricultural lien is first perfected, if there is no period thereafter when there is neither filing nor perfection.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-322(1)(b): A perfected security interest or agricultural lien has priority over a conflicting unperfected security interest or agricultural lien.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-322(1)(c): The first security interest or agricultural lien to attach or become effective has priority if conflicting security interests and agricultural liens are unperfected.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-322(2): (1)(a) For the purposes of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-322(2)(a): the time of filing or perfection as to a security interest in collateral is also the time of filing or perfection as to a security interest in proceeds; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-322(2)(b): the time of filing or perfection as to a security interest in collateral supported by a supporting obligation is also the time of filing or perfection as to a security interest in the supporting obligation.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-322(3): (6); 70A-9a-327; 70A-9a-328; 70A-9a-329; 70A-9a-330; 70A-9a-331 Except as otherwise provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-322(3)(a): any supporting obligation for the collateral; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-322(3)(b): proceeds of the collateral if:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-322(3)(b)(i): the security interest in proceeds is perfected;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-322(3)(b)(ii): the proceeds are cash proceeds or of the same type as the collateral; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-322(3)(b)(iii): in the case of proceeds that are proceeds of proceeds, all intervening proceeds are cash proceeds, proceeds of the same type as the collateral, or an account relating to the collateral.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-322(4): (5); (6) Subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-322(5): (4) Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-322(6): (1); (5); (7); 70A-4-210; 70A-5-118; 70A-9a-110; Chapter 2, Uniform Commercial Code - Sales; Chapter 2a, Uniform Commercial Code - Leases Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-322(6)(a): (7) Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-322(6)(b): 70A-4-210 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-322(6)(c): 70A-5-118 Section

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-332 Transfer of money -- Transfer of funds from deposit account.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-332(1): A transferee of money takes the money free of a security interest unless the transferee acts in collusion with the debtor in violating the rights of the secured party.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-332(2): A transferee of funds from a deposit account takes the funds free of a security interest in the deposit account unless the transferee acts in collusion with the debtor in violating the rights of the secured party.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-333 Priority of certain liens arising by operation of law.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-333(1): In this section, "possessory lien" means an interest, other than a security interest or an agricultural lien:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-333(1)(a): which secures payment or performance of an obligation for services or materials furnished with respect to goods by a person in the ordinary course of the person's business;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-333(1)(b): which is created by statute or rule of law in favor of the person; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-333(1)(c): whose effectiveness depends on the person's possession of the goods.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-333(2): A possessory lien on goods has priority over a security interest in the goods unless the lien is created by a statute that expressly provides otherwise.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-334 Priority of security interests in fixtures and crops.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-334(1): A security interest under this chapter may be created in goods that are fixtures or may continue in goods that become fixtures.  A security interest does not exist under this chapter in ordinary building materials incorporated into an improvement on land.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-334(2): This chapter does not prevent creation of an encumbrance upon fixtures under real property law.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-334(3): (4); (8) In cases not governed by Subsections

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-334(4)(c): the security interest is perfected by a fixture filing before the goods become fixtures or within 20 days thereafter.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-334(5)(b): before the goods become fixtures, the security interest is perfected by any method permitted by this chapter and the fixtures are readily removable:

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-336 Commingled goods.
--------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-336(1): In this section, "commingled goods" means goods that are physically united with other goods in such a manner that their identity is lost in a product or mass.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-336(2): A security interest does not exist in commingled goods as such.  However, a security interest may attach to a product or mass that results when goods become commingled goods.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-336(3): If collateral becomes commingled goods, a security interest attaches to the product or mass.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-336(4): (3) If a security interest in collateral is perfected before the collateral becomes commingled goods, the security interest that attaches to the product or mass under Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-336(6)(a): (4) A security interest that is perfected under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-336(6)(b): (4) If more than one security interest is perfected under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-337 Priority of security interests in goods covered by certificate of title.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
If, while a security interest in goods is perfected by any method under the law of another jurisdiction, this state issues a certificate of title that does not show that the goods are subject to the security interest or contain a statement that they may be subject to security interests not shown on the certificate:Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-337(1): a buyer of the goods, other than a person in the business of selling goods of that kind, takes free of the security interest if the buyer gives value and receives delivery of the goods after issuance of the certificate and without knowledge of the security interest; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-337(2): 70A-9a-311(2) the security interest is subordinate to a conflicting security interest in the goods that attaches, and is perfected under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-338 Priority of security interest or agricultural lien perfected by filed financing statement providing certain incorrect information.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
If a security interest or agricultural lien is perfected by a filed financing statement providing information described in SubsectionUtah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-338(1): the security interest or agricultural lien is subordinate to a conflicting perfected security interest in the collateral to the extent that the holder of the conflicting security interest gives value in reasonable reliance upon the incorrect information; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-338(2): a purchaser, other than a secured party, of the collateral takes free of the security interest or agricultural lien to the extent that, in reasonable reliance upon the incorrect information, the purchaser gives value and, in the case of tangible chattel paper, tangible documents, goods, instruments, or a security certificate, receives delivery of the collateral.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-339 Priority subject to subordination.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
This chapter does not preclude subordination by agreement by a person entitled to priority.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-402 Secured party not obligated on contract of debtor or in tort.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The existence of a security interest, agricultural lien, or authority given to a debtor to dispose of or use collateral, without more, does not subject a secured party to liability in contract or tort for the debtor's acts or omissions.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-409(1): A term in a letter of credit or a rule of law, statute, regulation, custom, or practice applicable to the letter of credit which prohibits, restricts, or requires the consent of an applicant, issuer, or nominated person to a beneficiary's assignment of or creation of a security interest in a letter-of-credit right is ineffective to the extent that the term or rule of law, statute, regulation, custom, or practice:

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-409(1)(b): provides that the assignment or the creation, attachment, or perfection of the security interest may give rise to a default, breach, right of recoupment, claim, defense, termination, right of termination, or remedy under the letter-of-credit right.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-409(2): (1) To the extent that a term in a letter of credit is ineffective under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-409(2)(a): is not enforceable against the applicant, issuer, nominated person, or transferee beneficiary;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-409(2)(b): imposes no duties or obligations on the applicant, issuer, nominated person, or transferee beneficiary; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-409(2)(c): does not require the applicant, issuer, nominated person, or transferee beneficiary to recognize the security interest, pay or render performance to the secured party, or accept payment or other performance from the secured party.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-513 Termination statement.
-------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-513(1): A secured party shall cause the secured party of record for a financing statement to file a termination statement for the financing statement if the financing statement covers consumer goods and:

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-513(1)(b): the debtor did not authorize the filing of the initial financing statement.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-513(2)(b): if earlier, within 20 days after the secured party receives an authenticated demand from a debtor.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-513(3): (1) In cases not governed by Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-513(3)(a): except in the case of a financing statement covering accounts or chattel paper that has been sold or goods that are the subject of a consignment, there is no obligation secured by the collateral covered by the financing statement and no commitment to make an advance, incur an obligation, or otherwise give value;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-513(3)(b): the financing statement covers accounts or chattel paper that has been sold but as to which the account debtor or other person obligated has discharged its obligation;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-513(3)(c): the financing statement covers goods that were the subject of a consignment to the debtor but are not in the debtor's possession; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-513(3)(d): the debtor did not authorize the filing of the initial financing statement.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-517 Effect of indexing errors.
-----------------------------------------------------------
The failure of the filing office to index a record correctly does not affect the effectiveness of the filed record.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-518(1): A person may file in the filing office an information statement with respect to a record indexed there under the person's name if the person believes that the record is inaccurate or was wrongfully filed.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-524 Delay by filing office.
--------------------------------------------------------
Delay by the filing office beyond a time limit prescribed by this part is excused if:Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-524(1): the delay is caused by interruption of communication or computer facilities, war, emergency conditions, failure of equipment, or other circumstances beyond control of the filing office; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-524(2): the filing office exercises reasonable diligence under the circumstances.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-526 Filing-office rules.
-----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-526(1): 70A-9a-501(1)(b); Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act The Division of Corporations and Commercial Code shall adopt and publish rules to implement this chapter that apply to a filing office described in Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-526(1)(b): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act adopted and published in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-526(2): To keep the filing-office rules and practices of the filing office in harmony with the rules and practices of filing offices in other jurisdictions that enact substantially this part, and to keep the technology used by the filing office compatible with the technology used by filing offices in other jurisdictions that enact substantially this part, the Division of Corporations and Commercial Code, so far as is consistent with the purposes, policies, and provisions of this chapter, in adopting, amending, and repealing filing-office rules, shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-526(2)(a): consult with filing offices in other jurisdictions that enact substantially this part;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-526(2)(b): consult the most recent version of the Model Rules promulgated by the International Association of Corporate Administrators or any successor organization; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-526(2)(c): take into consideration the rules and practices of, and the technology used by, filing offices in other jurisdictions that enact substantially this part.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-604 Procedure if security agreement covers real property or fixtures.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-604(1): If a security agreement covers both personal and real property, a secured party may proceed:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-604(1)(a): under this part as to the personal property without prejudicing any rights with respect to the real property; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-604(1)(b): as to both the personal property and the real property in accordance with the rights with respect to the real property, in which case the other provisions of this part do not apply.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-604(2): (3) Subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-604(2)(a): under this part; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-604(2)(b): in accordance with the rights with respect to real property, in which case the other provisions of this part do not apply.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-604(3): Subject to the other provisions of this part, if a secured party holding a security interest in fixtures has priority over all owners and encumbrancers of the real property, the secured party, after default, may remove the collateral from the real property.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-604(4): A secured party that removes collateral shall promptly reimburse any encumbrancer or owner of the real property, other than the debtor, for the cost of repair of any physical injury caused by the removal.  The secured party need not reimburse the encumbrancer or owner for any diminution in value of the real property caused by the absence of the goods removed or by any necessity of replacing them.  A person entitled to reimbursement may refuse permission to remove until the secured party gives adequate assurance for the performance of the obligation to reimburse.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-605 Unknown debtor or secondary obligor.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
A secured party does not owe a duty based on its status as secured party:Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-605(1): to a person that is a debtor or obligor, unless the secured party knows:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-605(1)(a): that the person is a debtor or obligor;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-605(1)(b): the identity of the person; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-605(1)(c): how to communicate with the person; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-605(2): to a secured party or lienholder that has filed a financing statement against a person, unless the secured party knows:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-605(2)(a): that the person is a debtor; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-605(2)(b): the identity of the person.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-606 Time of default for agricultural lien.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
For purposes of this part, a default occurs in connection with an agricultural lien at the time the secured party becomes entitled to enforce the lien in accordance with the statute under which it was created.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-608 Application of proceeds of collection or enforcement -- Liability for deficiency and right to surplus.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-608(1): 70A-9a-607; (1)(a)(iii); 70A-9a-607 If a security interest or agricultural lien secures payment or performance of an obligation, the following rules apply:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-608(1)(a): 70A-9a-607 A secured party shall apply or pay over for application the cash proceeds of collection or enforcement under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-608(1)(a)(i): the reasonable expenses of collection and enforcement and, to the extent provided for by agreement and not prohibited by law, reasonable attorney's fees and legal expenses incurred by the secured party;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-608(1)(a)(ii): the satisfaction of obligations secured by the security interest or agricultural lien under which the collection or enforcement is made; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-608(1)(a)(iii): the satisfaction of obligations secured by any subordinate security interest in or other lien on the collateral subject to the security interest or agricultural lien under which the collection or enforcement is made if the secured party receives an authenticated demand for proceeds before distribution of the proceeds is completed.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-608(1)(b): (1)(a)(iii) If requested by a secured party, a holder of a subordinate security interest or other lien shall furnish reasonable proof of the interest or lien within a reasonable time.  Unless the holder complies, the secured party need not comply with the holder's demand under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-608(1)(c): 70A-9a-607 A secured party need not apply or pay over for application noncash proceeds of collection and enforcement under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-608(1)(d): A secured party shall account to and pay a debtor for any surplus, and the obligor is liable for any deficiency.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-608(2): If the underlying transaction is a sale of accounts, chattel paper, payment intangibles, or promissory notes, the debtor is not entitled to any surplus, and the obligor is not liable for any deficiency.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-610 Disposition of collateral after default.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-610(1): After default, a secured party may sell, lease, license, or otherwise dispose of any or all of the collateral in its present condition or following any commercially reasonable preparation or processing.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-610(2): Every aspect of a disposition of collateral, including the method, manner, time, place, and other terms, must be commercially reasonable.  If commercially reasonable, a secured party may dispose of collateral by public or private proceedings, by one or more contracts, as a unit or in parcels, and at any time and place and on any terms.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-610(3): A secured party may purchase collateral:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-610(3)(a): at a public disposition; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-610(3)(b): at a private disposition only if the collateral is of a kind that is customarily sold on a recognized market or the subject of widely distributed standard price quotations.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-610(4): A contract for sale, lease, license, or other disposition includes the warranties relating to title, possession, quiet enjoyment, and the like which by operation of law accompany a voluntary disposition of property of the kind subject to the contract.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-610(5): (4) A secured party may disclaim or modify warranties under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-610(5)(a): in a manner that would be effective to disclaim or modify the warranties in a voluntary disposition of property of the kind subject to the contract of disposition; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-610(5)(b): by communicating to the purchaser a record evidencing the contract for disposition and including an express disclaimer or modification of the warranties.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-610(6): (5) A record is sufficient to disclaim warranties under Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-615 Application of proceeds of disposition -- Liability for deficiency and right to surplus.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-615(1): 70A-9a-610 A secured party shall apply or pay over for application the cash proceeds of disposition under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-615(1)(a): the reasonable expenses of retaking, holding, preparing for disposition, processing, and disposing, and, to the extent provided for by agreement and not prohibited by law, reasonable attorney's fees and legal expenses incurred by the secured party;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-615(1)(b): the satisfaction of obligations secured by the security interest or agricultural lien under which the disposition is made;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-615(1)(c): the satisfaction of obligations secured by any subordinate security interest in or other subordinate lien on the collateral if:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-615(1)(c)(i): the secured party receives from the holder of the subordinate security interest or other lien an authenticated demand for proceeds before distribution of the proceeds is completed; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-615(1)(c)(ii): in a case in which a consignor has an interest in the collateral, the subordinate security interest or other lien is senior to the interest of the consignor; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-615(1)(d): a secured party that is a consignor of the collateral if the secured party receives from the consignor an authenticated demand for proceeds before distribution of the proceeds is completed.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-615(2): (1)(c) If requested by a secured party, a holder of a subordinate security interest or other lien shall furnish reasonable proof of the interest or lien within a reasonable time.  Unless the holder does so, the secured party need not comply with the holder's demand under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-615(3): 70A-9a-610 A secured party need not apply or pay over for application noncash proceeds of disposition under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-615(4): (1); (3); (1)(d) If the security interest under which a disposition is made secures payment or performance of an obligation, after making the payments and applications required by Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-615(4)(a): (1)(d) unless Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-615(4)(b): the obligor is liable for any deficiency.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-615(5): If the underlying transaction is a sale of accounts, chattel paper, payment intangibles, or promissory notes:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-615(5)(a): the debtor is not entitled to any surplus; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-615(5)(b): the obligor is not liable for any deficiency.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-615(6): The surplus or deficiency following a disposition is calculated based on the amount of proceeds that would have been realized in a disposition complying with this part to a transferee other than the secured party, a person related to the secured party, or a secondary obligor if:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-615(6)(a): the transferee in the disposition is the secured party, a person related to the secured party, or a secondary obligor; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-615(6)(b): the amount of proceeds of the disposition is significantly below the range of proceeds that a complying disposition to a person other than the secured party, a person related to the secured party, or a secondary obligor would have brought.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-615(7): A secured party that receives cash proceeds of a disposition in good faith and without knowledge that the receipt violates the rights of the holder of a security interest or other lien that is not subordinate to the security interest or agricultural lien under which the disposition is made:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-615(7)(a): takes the cash proceeds free of the security interest or other lien;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-615(7)(b): is not obligated to apply the proceeds of the disposition to the satisfaction of obligations secured by the security interest or other lien; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-615(7)(c): is not obligated to account to or pay the holder of the security interest or other lien for any surplus.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-617 Rights of transferee of collateral.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-617(1): A secured party's disposition of collateral after default:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-617(1)(a): transfers to a transferee for value all of the debtor's rights in the collateral;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-617(1)(b): discharges the security interest under which the disposition is made; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-617(1)(c): discharges any subordinate security interest or other subordinate lien.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-617(2): (1) A transferee that acts in good faith takes free of the rights and interests described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-617(3): (1) If a transferee does not take free of the rights and interests described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-617(3)(a): the debtor's rights in the collateral;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-617(3)(b): the security interest or agricultural lien under which the disposition is made; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-617(3)(c): any other security interest or other lien.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-618 Rights and duties of certain secondary obligors.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-618(1): A secondary obligor acquires the rights and becomes obligated to perform the duties of the secured party after the secondary obligor:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-618(1)(a): receives an assignment of a secured obligation from the secured party;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-618(1)(b): receives a transfer of collateral from the secured party and agrees to accept the rights and assume the duties of the secured party; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-618(1)(c): is subrogated to the rights of a secured party with respect to collateral.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-618(2): (1); 70A-9a-610 An assignment, transfer, or subrogation described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-618(2)(a): 70A-9a-610 is not a disposition of collateral under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-618(2)(b): relieves the secured party of further duties under this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-619 Transfer of record or legal title.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-619(1): In this section, "transfer statement" means a record authenticated by a secured party stating:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-619(1)(a): that the debtor has defaulted in connection with an obligation secured by specified collateral;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-619(1)(b): that the secured party has exercised its post-default remedies with respect to the collateral;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-619(1)(c): that, by reason of the exercise, a transferee has acquired the rights of the debtor in the collateral; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-619(1)(d): the name and mailing address of the secured party, debtor, and transferee.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-619(2): A transfer statement entitles the transferee to the transfer of record of all rights of the debtor in the collateral specified in the statement in any official filing, recording, registration, or certificate-of-title system covering the collateral.  If a transfer statement is presented with the applicable fee and request form to the official or office responsible for maintaining the system, the official or office shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-619(2)(a): accept the transfer statement;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-619(2)(b): promptly amend its records to reflect the transfer; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-619(2)(c): if applicable, issue a new appropriate certificate of title in the name of the transferee.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-619(3): (2) A transfer of the record or legal title to collateral to a secured party under Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-622 Effect of acceptance of collateral.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-622(1): A secured party's acceptance of collateral in full or partial satisfaction of the obligation it secures:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-622(1)(a): discharges the obligation to the extent consented to by the debtor;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-622(1)(b): transfers to the secured party all of a debtor's rights in the collateral;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-622(1)(c): discharges the security interest or agricultural lien that is the subject of the debtor's consent and any subordinate security interest or other subordinate lien; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-622(1)(d): terminates any other subordinate interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-622(2): (1) A subordinate interest is discharged or terminated under Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-627 Determination of whether conduct was commercially reasonable.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-627(1): The fact that a greater amount could have been obtained by a collection, enforcement, disposition, or acceptance at a different time or in a different method from that selected by the secured party is not of itself sufficient to preclude the secured party from establishing that the collection, enforcement, disposition, or acceptance was made in a commercially reasonable manner.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-627(2): A disposition of collateral is made in a commercially reasonable manner if the disposition is made:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-627(2)(a): in the usual manner on any recognized market;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-627(2)(b): at the price current in any recognized market at the time of the disposition; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-627(2)(c): otherwise in conformity with reasonable commercial practices among dealers in the type of property that was the subject of the disposition.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-627(3): A collection, enforcement, disposition, or acceptance is commercially reasonable if it has been approved:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-627(3)(a): in a judicial proceeding;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-627(3)(b): by a bona fide creditors' committee;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-627(3)(c): by a representative of creditors; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-627(3)(d): by an assignee for the benefit of creditors.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-627(4): (3) Approval under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-628 Nonliability and limitation on liability of secured party -- Liability of secondary obligor.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-628(1): Unless a secured party knows that a person is a debtor or obligor, knows the identity of the person, and knows how to communicate with the person:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-628(1)(a): the secured party is not liable to the person, or to a secured party or lienholder that has filed a financing statement against the person, for failure to comply with this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-628(1)(b): the secured party's failure to comply with this chapter does not affect the liability of the person for a deficiency.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-628(2): A secured party is not liable because of its status as secured party:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-628(2)(a): to a person that is a debtor or obligor, unless the secured party knows:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-628(2)(a)(i): that the person is a debtor or obligor;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-628(2)(a)(ii): the identity of the person; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-628(2)(a)(iii): how to communicate with the person; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-628(2)(b): to a secured party or lienholder that has filed a financing statement against a person, unless the secured party knows:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-628(2)(b)(i): that the person is a debtor; and
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-628(2)(b)(ii): the identity of the person.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-628(3): A secured party is not liable to any person, and a person's liability for a deficiency is not affected, because of any act or omission arising out of the secured party's reasonable belief that a transaction is not a consumer-goods transaction or a consumer transaction or that goods are not consumer goods, if the secured party's belief is based on its reasonable reliance on:
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-628(3)(a): a debtor's representation concerning the purpose for which collateral was to be used, acquired, or held; or
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-628(3)(b): an obligor's representation concerning the purpose for which a secured obligation was incurred.
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-628(4): 70A-9a-625(3)(b); 70A-9a-616 A secured party is not liable to any person under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-628(5): 70A-9a-625(3)(b) A secured party is not liable under Section

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-9a-708(2)(b): to perfect or continue the perfection of a security interest.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 70A - Chapter 10 - Effective Date and Repealer
**************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-10-101 Effective date.
------------------------------------------------
This act shall become effective at midnight on December 31st, 1965. It applies to transactions entered into and events occurring after that date.

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-10-102 Specific repealer -- Provision for transition.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-10-102(1): The following acts and all other acts and parts of acts inconsistent herewith are hereby repealed:

Utah Code Annotated § 70A-10-102(1)(c): Uniform Sales Act, Title 60, U.C.A., 1953;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-10-102(1)(d): Uniform Stock Transfer Act, Title 16, Chapter 3, U.C.A., 1953;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-10-102(1)(e): Uniform Trust Receipts Act, Title 9, Chapter 2, U.C.A., 1953;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-10-102(1)(f): Title 9, Chapter 1, U.C.A., 1953;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-10-102(1)(g): Title 9, Chapter 3, U.C.A., 1953;
Utah Code Annotated § 70A-10-102(1)(h): Title 25, Chapter 2, U.C.A., 1953;
